## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate-law ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard formulation of reaction kinetics via rate laws. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are ODE rate laws where the reaction rate depends on A (reaction order, saturation, equilibrium) and possibly explicit time-dependence capturing changing conditions (e.g., catalyst deactivation, temperature/programmed forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion; surface-limited or saturated catalyst)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition under fixed conditions)
- Second-order decay (single-species): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A -> products, or recombination)
- nth-order power-law rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order, including fractional orders)
- Reversible/relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1 with rate c0)
- Source + first-order sink (CSTR-like forcing): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant production/feed with linear removal/decay)
- Autocatalytic (self-accelerating then self-limiting): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type kinetics from autocatalysis/limited resource)
- Saturation/inhibition in the rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to site limitation/inhibition)
- Generalized saturation with reaction order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (transition from low-A power law to high-A plateau in rate magnitude)
- Time-dependent (deactivating) first-order: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate decreases over time; catalyst deactivation or cooling program)
- Time-dependent (power-law) first-order: dA_dt = -c0 * (t + c1)**c2 * A (rate changes with time due to aging/mixing/temperature ramps)
- Periodic forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (concentration driven by periodic feed/irradiation while decaying)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption-only reactions typically enforce dA_dt Ōēż 0 for A Ōēź 0, suggesting leading negative terms like -c*A**n.
- Reaction order manifests as curvature in log(-dA_dt) vs log(A): linear trend implies power-law dA_dt = -c*A**n.
- Approach to a nonzero steady state indicates a relaxation form dA_dt ŌłØ -(A - A_eq), yielding a stable fixed point at A = A_eq.
- If the apparent rate slows as A grows (site limitation/inhibition), use rational forms like -c*A/(A+c) to plateau the rate magnitude.
- Self-accelerating early-time behavior followed by slowdown suggests autocatalytic structure A*(const - A), producing an internal maximum of dA_dt vs A.
- Changes in conditions over time (temperature drift, catalyst deactivation) often appear as multiplicative time factors on the rate constant, e.g., exp(-c*t) or (t+c)**p.
- External driving (feed/illumination) produces additive source terms in dA_dt, e.g., +c or +c*sin(c*t), superimposed on decay terms.
- Finite-time depletion under constant-rate or strong nonlinearity can be captured by zero-order (-c0) or higher-order (-c*A**n, n>1) kinetics depending on observed tail behavior.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK34)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_f*A**c3
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function (independent of `t`):
\[
GT(A)=0.7240016388253205\,A^{1/3}-0.1689114325901851\,A^2.
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) have **no actual dependence on `t`** after parameter choice, and (ii) equal a **sum of exactly two power terms** in \(A\): one \(A^2\) term with coefficient \(-0.1689...\) and one \(A^{1/3}\) term with coefficient \(0.7240...\). Any extra functional forms (rational \(A/(A+c)\), logs, sin, exp in \(A\), Max, etc.) must be removable by setting their coefficients to 0; but if the candidate has no way to produce an \(A^{1/3}\) term (only linear/rational/log/etc.), it cannot match.

---

### 1.
Contains linear-in-\(A\) terms, \(A/(A+c4)\), and \(t\)-exp term. You can zero out exp and constants, but you still canŌĆÖt create \(A^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### 2.
Has \(A^2 c0\) plus a rational power term \(A^{c1}c2/(A^{c1}+c3)\) and exponentials in \(t\). Kill \(t\)-terms by setting \(c4=c7=0\). Remaining rational term cannot equal \(kA^{1/3}\) for all \(A\) (it behaves like \(c2\) for large \(A\) if \(c3\neq0\), or constant if \(c3=0\)). Not a pure power. **No match**.

### 3.
Same rational term issue; also has \(A^{c4}c5\exp(c6 t)\). To remove \(t\), set \(c6=0\) so \(\exp(0)=1\), leaving \(A^{c4}c5\), which *could* make \(A^{1/3}\). But the rational term \(A^{c1}c2/(A^{c1}+c3)\) must vanish: set \(c2=0\). Then candidate becomes \(A^2 c0 + c5 A^{c4}\). Choose
- \(c0=-0.1689114325901851\)
- \(c4=1/3\)
- \(c5=0.7240016388253205\)
This matches GT exactly. **Match**.

### 4.
Has rational term plus \(c4\exp(Ac5)\). Exponential in \(A\) cannot become a power \(A^{1/3}\) for all \(A\) unless coefficient is 0. If set \(c4=0\), left with \(A^2 c0 +\) rational term; rational term cannot be \(A^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### 5.
Has \(A c1 e^{c2 t}\), rational term, and \(\log(Ac7+1)\). To remove \(t\), need \(c1=0\) or \(c2=0\) (but then itŌĆÖs linear in \(A\)). Log cannot become \(A^{1/3}\). Rational term not pure power. **No match**.

### 6.
Has rational term, plus \(A^{c4}c5\) (good), plus \(c6 e^{A c7}\) (must set \(c6=0\)). Still must remove rational term by \(c2=0\). Then becomes \(A^2 c0 + c5 A^{c4}\), which can match GT with same settings as in (3). **Match**.

### 7.
Has rational term and an oscillatory \(e^{c5 t}\sin(...)\). Must set \(c4=0\) to remove it; then still rational term canŌĆÖt produce \(A^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### 8.
Has linear terms, \(A/(A+c4)\), and \(A^{c5}c6\log(Ac7+1)\). Log factor prevents pure power unless \(c6=0\). Then no \(A^{1/3}\) source. **No match**.

### 9.
Has rational term, plus \(A^{c4}c5\) (good), plus log term (set \(c6=0\)). Still must kill rational term via \(c2=0\). Then \(A^2 c0 + c5 A^{c4}\) matches GT by choosing \(c0, c4, c5\) as above. **Match**.

### 10.
Only polynomial-ish terms plus \(A/(A+c4)\) and \(t\)-exp. No \(A^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### 11.
Only rational-in-\(A\), sin in \(A\), log. No way to get \(A^{1/3}\) and \(A^2\) simultaneously as pure powers. **No match**.

### 12.
Has \(A^2 c0\), linear term, and a rational term involving \(e^{c4 t}\). Can remove \(t\) by setting \(c4=0\), but still only linear/rational; no \(A^{1/3}\). **No match**.

### 13.

### 14.

### 15.

### 16.

### 18.

### 19.

### 29.

### 34.
\(A^{c0}c1 + c2*Max(0,A)^{c3} + c4\).
